## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of concentration dA/dt as a function of time and concentration, which is the fundamental problem in chemical kinetics â€” determining the rate law. The rate typically depends on concentration through power-law or rational expressions, and may have explicit time dependence for complex or externally driven reactions.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to square of concentration)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate dependence)
- First-order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (first-order with constant source/sink)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * (c2 - A) (forward and reverse first-order reactions)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme or saturation kinetics)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalytic reaction)
- Second-order mixed: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A)**c2 (generalized autocatalytic kinetics)
- Time-dependent rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying rate constant)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition)
- Competitive saturation: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 / (c1 + A) (second-order with saturation)
- Fractional order with equilibrium: dA_dt = c0 * (A**c1 - c2) (approach to equilibrium)
- Combined polynomial: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 + c2 * A**3 (complex multi-step mechanism)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservation of mass constraints â†’ rate expressions often contain terms like (c - A) representing depletion of a co-reactant or approach to equilibrium
- Enzyme/catalyst saturation â†’ rational forms A/(c+A) or A**n/(c+A**n) arise from quasi-steady-state approximations of intermediate species
- Autocatalytic feedback â†’ product terms A*(c-A) indicate the product catalyzes its own formation from a fixed total pool
- Competing reaction pathways â†’ sums of power-law terms c0*A**n1 + c1*A**n2 represent parallel reaction channels
- Approach to equilibrium â†’ expressions like c0*(A - c1) where c1 represents the equilibrium concentration drive the system toward steady state
- Cooperative kinetics â†’ Hill-type terms A**n/(c + A**n) with n>1 indicate cooperative binding or multi-molecular steps
- Chain reaction mechanisms â†’ square root dependence A**0.5 arises from radical chain termination balancing initiation
- Pseudo-first-order simplification â†’ when one reactant is in excess, multi-species rate laws reduce to single-variable power laws in A
